                                 SENATE FILE

 A BILL FOR

  1 An Act extending the limitations of certain criminal actions
  2    committed on or with minors, and providing penalties.
  3 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA:

    jm/rj

  1  2 amended to read as follows:
  1  3    1.  An information or indictment for sexual abuse in the
  1  4 first, second, or third degree committed on or with a person
  1  5 who is under the age of eighteen years

  3 11 person's DNA profile.  3 11 person's DNA profile.  3 12                           EXPLANATION
  3 13 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3 14 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 15    This bill extends the limitations of certain criminal
  3 16 actions (statute of limitations) committed on or with minors.
  3 17    The amendment to Code section 802.2 provides that an
  3 18 information or indictment for sexual abuse in the first,
  3 19 second, or third degree committed on or with a person who
  3 20 is under the age of 18 years may be found at any time after
  3 21 commission of the offense. Under current law, an information
  3 22 or indictment for a sexual abuse offense committed on or with
  3 23 a person who is under 18 years of age shall be found within
  3 24 10 years after the person upon whom the offense is committed
  3 25 attains 18 years of age, or if the person against whom the
  3 26 information or indictment is sought is identified through the
  3 27 use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment shall be
  3 28 found within three years from the date the person is identified
  3 29 by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  3 30    The amendment to Code section 802.2A provides that an
  3 31 information or indictment for incest under Code section 726.2
  3 32 committed on or with a person who is under the age of 18 may
  3 33 be found at any time after commission of the offense.  Under
  3 34 current law, an information or indictment for incest shall be
  3 35 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  4  1 is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other incest
  4  2 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older,
  4  3 the information or indictment shall be found within 10 years
  4  4 after the commission of the offense.  If the person against
  4  5 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  4  6 only through the use of a DNA profile, the limitation shall be
  4  7 tolled.  However, an information or indictment shall be found
  4  8 within three years from the date the person is identified by
  4  9 the person's DNA profile.
  4 10    The amendment to Code section 802.2A also provides that
  4 11 an information or indictment for sexual exploitation by a
  4 12 counselor, therapist, or school employee under Code section
  4 13 709.15 committed on or with a person who is under the age of
  4 14 18 may be found at any time after commission of the offense.
  4 15 Under current law, an information or indictment for sexual
  4 16 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee
  4 17 shall be found within 10 years after the person upon whom the
  4 18 offense is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other sexual
  4 19 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee
  4 20 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older, the
  4 21 information or indictment shall be found within 10 years of the
  4 22 date the person was last treated by the counselor or therapist,
  4 23 or within 10 years of the date the person was enrolled in or
  4 24 attended the school.
  4 25    The amendment to Code section 802.2B provides that an
  4 26 information or indictment may be commenced at any time after
  4 27 the commission of any of the following offenses if the offense
  4 28 is committed on or with a person under the age of 18: sexual
  4 29 abuse in the first degree in violation of Code section 709.2;
  4 30 sexual abuse in the second degree in violation of Code section
  4 31 709.3; sexual abuse in the third degree in violation of Code
  4 32 section 709.4; lascivious acts with a child in violation of
  4 33 Code section 709.8; assault with intent to commit sexual abuse
  4 34 in violation of Code section 709.11; indecent contact with a
  4 35 child in violation of Code section 709.12; lascivious conduct
  5  1 with a minor in violation of Code section 709.14; sexual
  5  2 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee in
  5  3 violation of Code section 709.15; sexual misconduct with a
  5  4 juvenile in violation of Code section 709.16, subsection 2;
  5  5 kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Code section
  5  6 710.2; kidnapping in the second degree in violation of Code
  5  7 section 710.3; kidnapping in the third degree in violation of
  5  8 Code section 710.4; human trafficking in violation of Code
  5  9 section 710A.2; incest in violation of Code section 726.2; and
  5 10 sexual exploitation of a minor in violation of Code section
  5 11 728.12. Under current law for the preceding offenses, an
  5 12 information or indictment  committed on or with a person who
  5 13 is under 18 years of age shall be found within 10 years after
  5 14 the person upon whom the offense is committed attains 18 years
  5 15 of age, or if the person against whom the information or
  5 16 indictment is sought is identified through the use of a DNA
  5 17 profile, an information or indictment shall be found within
  5 18 three years from the date the person is identified by the
  5 19 person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 20    The amendment to Code section 802.2C provides that an
  5 21 information or indictment for kidnapping in the first, second,
  5 22 or third degree committed on or with a person who is under the
  5 23 age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  5 24 the offense. Under current law for kidnapping offenses, the
  5 25 information or indictment for an offense committed on or with
  5 26 a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  5 27 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  5 28 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  5 29 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  5 30 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  5 31 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  5 32 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 33    The amendment to Code section 802.2D provides that an
  5 34 information or indictment for human trafficking in violation of
  5 35 Code section 710A.2, committed on or with a person who is under
  6  1 the age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  6  2 the offense. Under current law for human trafficking offenses,
  6  3 the information or indictment for an offense committed on or
  6  4 with a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  6  5 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  6  6 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  6  7 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  6  8 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  6  9 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  6 10 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  6 11    The amendment to Code section 802.10 makes conforming
  6 12 changes to comply with the changes in the bill.
       LSB 1641XS (15) 87
       jm/rj
  3 13 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3 14 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 15    This bill extends the limitations of certain criminal
  3 16 actions (statute of limitations) committed on or with minors.
  3 17    The amendment to Code section 802.2 provides that an
  3 18 information or indictment for sexual abuse in the first,
  3 19 second, or third degree committed on or with a person who
  3 20 is under the age of 18 years may be found at any time after
  3 21 commission of the offense. Under current law, an information

  3 26 information or indictment is sought is identified through the
  3 27 use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment shall be
  3 28 found within three years from the date the person is identified
  3 29 by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  3 30    The amendment to Code section 802.2A provides that an
  3 31 information or indictment for incest under Code section 726.2
  3 32 committed on or with a person who is under the age of 18 may
  3 33 be found at any time after commission of the offense.  Under
  3 34 current law, an information or indictment for incest shall be
  3 35 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  4  1 is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other incest
  4  2 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older,
  4  3 the information or indictment shall be found within 10 years
  4  4 after the commission of the offense.  If the person against
  4  5 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  4  6 only through the use of a DNA profile, the limitation shall be
  4  7 tolled.  However, an information or indictment shall be found
  4  8 within three years from the date the person is identified by
  4  9 the person's DNA profile.
  4 10    The amendment to Code section 802.2A also provides that
  4 11 an information or indictment for sexual exploitation by a
  4 12 counselor, therapist, or school employee under Code section
  4 13 709.15 committed on or with a person who is under the age of
  4 14 18 may be found at any time after commission of the offense.
  4 15 Under current law, an information or indictment for sexual
  4 16 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee
  4 17 shall be found within 10 years after the person upon whom the
  4 18 offense is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other sexual

  4 20 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older, the
  4 21 information or indictment shall be found within 10 years of the
  4 22 date the person was last treated by the counselor or therapist,
  4 23 or within 10 years of the date the person was enrolled in or
  4 24 attended the school.
  4 25    The amendment to Code section 802.2B provides that an
  4 26 information or indictment may be commenced at any time after
  4 27 the commission of any of the following offenses if the offense
  4 28 is committed on or with a person under the age of 18: sexual
  4 29 abuse in the first degree in violation of Code section 709.2;
  4 30 sexual abuse in the second degree in violation of Code section
  4 31 709.3; sexual abuse in the third degree in violation of Code
  4 32 section 709.4; lascivious acts with a child in violation of
  4 33 Code section 709.8; assault with intent to commit sexual abuse
  4 34 in violation of Code section 709.11; indecent contact with a
  4 35 child in violation of Code section 709.12; lascivious conduct
  5  1 with a minor in violation of Code section 709.14; sexual
  5  2 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee in
  5  3 violation of Code section 709.15; sexual misconduct with a
  5  4 juvenile in violation of Code section 709.16, subsection 2;
  5  5 kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Code section
  5  6 710.2; kidnapping in the second degree in violation of Code
  5  7 section 710.3; kidnapping in the third degree in violation of
  5  8 Code section 710.4; human trafficking in violation of Code
  5  9 section 710A.2; incest in violation of Code section 726.2; and
  5 10 sexual exploitation of a minor in violation of Code section
  5 11 728.12. Under current law for the preceding offenses, an
  5 12 information or indictment  committed on or with a person who
  5 13 is under 18 years of age shall be found within 10 years after
  5 14 the person upon whom the offense is committed attains 18 years
  5 15 of age, or if the person against whom the information or
  5 16 indictment is sought is identified through the use of a DNA
  5 17 profile, an information or indictment shall be found within
  5 18 three years from the date the person is identified by the
  5 19 person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 20    The amendment to Code section 802.2C provides that an
  5 21 information or indictment for kidnapping in the first, second,
  5 22 or third degree committed on or with a person who is under the
  5 23 age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  5 24 the offense. Under current law for kidnapping offenses, the
  5 25 information or indictment for an offense committed on or with
  5 26 a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  5 27 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  5 28 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  5 29 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  5 30 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  5 31 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  5 32 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 33    The amendment to Code section 802.2D provides that an
  5 34 information or indictment for human trafficking in violation of
  5 35 Code section 710A.2, committed on or with a person who is under
  6  1 the age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  6  2 the offense. Under current law for human trafficking offenses,
  6  3 the information or indictment for an offense committed on or
  6  4 with a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  6  5 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  6  6 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  6  7 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  6  8 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  6  9 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  6 10 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  6 11    The amendment to Code section 802.10 makes conforming
  6 12 changes to comply with the changes in the bill.
       LSB 1641XS (15) 87
       jm/rj
  3 14 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 15    This bill extends the limitations of certain criminal
  3 16 actions (statute of limitations) committed on or with minors.
  3 17    The amendment to Code section 802.2 provides that an
  3 18 information or indictment for sexual abuse in the first,
  3 19 second, or third degree committed on or with a person who
  3 20 is under the age of 18 years may be found at any time after
  3 21 commission of the offense. Under current law, an information
  3 22 or indictment for a sexual abuse offense committed on or with
  3 23 a person who is under 18 years of age shall be found within
  3 24 10 years after the person upon whom the offense is committed
  3 25 attains 18 years of age, or if the person against whom the
  3 26 information or indictment is sought is identified through the
  3 27 use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment shall be
  3 28 found within three years from the date the person is identified
  3 29 by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  3 30    The amendment to Code section 802.2A provides that an
  3 31 information or indictment for incest under Code section 726.2
  3 32 committed on or with a person who is under the age of 18 may
  3 33 be found at any time after commission of the offense.  Under
  3 34 current law, an information or indictment for incest shall be
  3 35 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  4  1 is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other incest
  4  2 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older,
  4  3 the information or indictment shall be found within 10 years
  4  4 after the commission of the offense.  If the person against
  4  5 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  4  6 only through the use of a DNA profile, the limitation shall be
  4  7 tolled.  However, an information or indictment shall be found
  4  8 within three years from the date the person is identified by
  4  9 the person's DNA profile.
  4 10    The amendment to Code section 802.2A also provides that
  4 11 an information or indictment for sexual exploitation by a
  4 12 counselor, therapist, or school employee under Code section
  4 13 709.15 committed on or with a person who is under the age of
  4 14 18 may be found at any time after commission of the offense.
  4 15 Under current law, an information or indictment for sexual
  4 16 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee
  4 17 shall be found within 10 years after the person upon whom the
  4 18 offense is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other sexual
  4 19 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee
  4 20 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older, the
  4 21 information or indictment shall be found within 10 years of the
  4 22 date the person was last treated by the counselor or therapist,
  4 23 or within 10 years of the date the person was enrolled in or
  4 24 attended the school.
  4 25    The amendment to Code section 802.2B provides that an
  4 26 information or indictment may be commenced at any time after
  4 27 the commission of any of the following offenses if the offense
  4 28 is committed on or with a person under the age of 18: sexual
  4 29 abuse in the first degree in violation of Code section 709.2;
  4 30 sexual abuse in the second degree in violation of Code section
  4 31 709.3; sexual abuse in the third degree in violation of Code
  4 32 section 709.4; lascivious acts with a child in violation of
  4 33 Code section 709.8; assault with intent to commit sexual abuse
  4 34 in violation of Code section 709.11; indecent contact with a
  4 35 child in violation of Code section 709.12; lascivious conduct
  5  1 with a minor in violation of Code section 709.14; sexual
  5  2 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee in
  5  3 violation of Code section 709.15; sexual misconduct with a
  5  4 juvenile in violation of Code section 709.16, subsection 2;
  5  5 kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Code section
  5  6 710.2; kidnapping in the second degree in violation of Code
  5  7 section 710.3; kidnapping in the third degree in violation of
  5  8 Code section 710.4; human trafficking in violation of Code
  5  9 section 710A.2; incest in violation of Code section 726.2; and
  5 10 sexual exploitation of a minor in violation of Code section
  5 11 728.12. Under current law for the preceding offenses, an
  5 12 information or indictment  committed on or with a person who
  5 13 is under 18 years of age shall be found within 10 years after
  5 14 the person upon whom the offense is committed attains 18 years
  5 15 of age, or if the person against whom the information or
  5 16 indictment is sought is identified through the use of a DNA
  5 17 profile, an information or indictment shall be found within
  5 18 three years from the date the person is identified by the
  5 19 person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 20    The amendment to Code section 802.2C provides that an
  5 21 information or indictment for kidnapping in the first, second,
  5 22 or third degree committed on or with a person who is under the
  5 23 age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  5 24 the offense. Under current law for kidnapping offenses, the
  5 25 information or indictment for an offense committed on or with
  5 26 a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  5 27 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  5 28 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  5 29 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  5 30 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  5 31 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  5 32 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 33    The amendment to Code section 802.2D provides that an
  5 34 information or indictment for human trafficking in violation of
  5 35 Code section 710A.2, committed on or with a person who is under
  6  1 the age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  6  2 the offense. Under current law for human trafficking offenses,
  6  3 the information or indictment for an offense committed on or
  6  4 with a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  6  5 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  6  6 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  6  7 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  6  8 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  6  9 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  6 10 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  6 11    The amendment to Code section 802.10 makes conforming
  6 12 changes to comply with the changes in the bill.

  3 23 a person who is under 18 years of age shall be found within
  3 24 10 years after the person upon whom the offense is committed
  3 25 attains 18 years of age, or if the person against whom the
  3 26 information or indictment is sought is identified through the
  3 27 use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment shall be
  3 28 found within three years from the date the person is identified
  3 29 by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  3 30    The amendment to Code section 802.2A provides that an
  3 31 information or indictment for incest under Code section 726.2
  3 32 committed on or with a person who is under the age of 18 may
  3 33 be found at any time after commission of the offense.  Under
  3 34 current law, an information or indictment for incest shall be
  3 35 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  4  1 is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other incest
  4  2 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older,
  4  3 the information or indictment shall be found within 10 years
  4  4 after the commission of the offense.  If the person against
  4  5 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  4  6 only through the use of a DNA profile, the limitation shall be
  4  7 tolled.  However, an information or indictment shall be found
  4  8 within three years from the date the person is identified by
  4  9 the person's DNA profile.

  4 11 an information or indictment for sexual exploitation by a
  4 12 counselor, therapist, or school employee under Code section
  4 13 709.15 committed on or with a person who is under the age of
  4 14 18 may be found at any time after commission of the offense.
  4 15 Under current law, an information or indictment for sexual

  4 17 shall be found within 10 years after the person upon whom the
  4 18 offense is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other sexual
  4 19 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee
  4 20 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older, the
  4 21 information or indictment shall be found within 10 years of the
  4 22 date the person was last treated by the counselor or therapist,
  4 23 or within 10 years of the date the person was enrolled in or
  4 24 attended the school.

  5 28 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  5 29 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  5 30 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  5 31 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  5 32 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 33    The amendment to Code section 802.2D provides that an
  5 34 information or indictment for human trafficking in violation of
  5 35 Code section 710A.2, committed on or with a person who is under
  6  1 the age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  6  2 the offense. Under current law for human trafficking offenses,
  6  3 the information or indictment for an offense committed on or
  6  4 with a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be

  6  8 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment

  3 30    The amendment to Code section 802.2A provides that an
  3 31 information or indictment for incest under Code section 726.2
  3 32 committed on or with a person who is under the age of 18 may
  3 33 be found at any time after commission of the offense.  Under
  3 34 current law, an information or indictment for incest shall be
  3 35 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  4  1 is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other incest
  4  2 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older,
  4  3 the information or indictment shall be found within 10 years
  4  4 after the commission of the offense.  If the person against
  4  5 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  4  6 only through the use of a DNA profile, the limitation shall be
  4  7 tolled.  However, an information or indictment shall be found
  4  8 within three years from the date the person is identified by
  4  9 the person's DNA profile.
  4 10    The amendment to Code section 802.2A also provides that
  4 11 an information or indictment for sexual exploitation by a
  4 12 counselor, therapist, or school employee under Code section
  4 13 709.15 committed on or with a person who is under the age of
  4 14 18 may be found at any time after commission of the offense.
  4 15 Under current law, an information or indictment for sexual
  4 16 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee
  4 17 shall be found within 10 years after the person upon whom the
  4 18 offense is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other sexual
  4 19 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee
  4 20 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older, the
  4 21 information or indictment shall be found within 10 years of the
  4 22 date the person was last treated by the counselor or therapist,
  4 23 or within 10 years of the date the person was enrolled in or
  4 24 attended the school.

  3 33 be found at any time after commission of the offense.  Under
  3 34 current law, an information or indictment for incest shall be
  3 35 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  4  1 is committed attains 18 years of age.  For other incest
  4  2 offenses committed upon a person 18 years of age or older,
  4  3 the information or indictment shall be found within 10 years
  4  4 after the commission of the offense.  If the person against
  4  5 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  4  6 only through the use of a DNA profile, the limitation shall be
  4  7 tolled.  However, an information or indictment shall be found
  4  8 within three years from the date the person is identified by
  4  9 the person's DNA profile.

  5 18 three years from the date the person is identified by the
  5 19 person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 20    The amendment to Code section 802.2C provides that an
  5 21 information or indictment for kidnapping in the first, second,
  5 22 or third degree committed on or with a person who is under the
  5 23 age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  5 24 the offense. Under current law for kidnapping offenses, the
  5 25 information or indictment for an offense committed on or with
  5 26 a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  5 27 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  5 28 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  5 29 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  5 30 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  5 31 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  5 32 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 33    The amendment to Code section 802.2D provides that an
  5 34 information or indictment for human trafficking in violation of
  5 35 Code section 710A.2, committed on or with a person who is under
  6  1 the age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  6  2 the offense. Under current law for human trafficking offenses,
  6  3 the information or indictment for an offense committed on or
  6  4 with a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  6  5 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  6  6 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  6  7 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  6  8 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  6  9 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  6 10 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  6 11    The amendment to Code section 802.10 makes conforming
  6 12 changes to comply with the changes in the bill.

  4 23 or within 10 years of the date the person was enrolled in or
  4 24 attended the school.
  4 25    The amendment to Code section 802.2B provides that an
  4 26 information or indictment may be commenced at any time after
  4 27 the commission of any of the following offenses if the offense
  4 28 is committed on or with a person under the age of 18: sexual
  4 29 abuse in the first degree in violation of Code section 709.2;
  4 30 sexual abuse in the second degree in violation of Code section
  4 31 709.3; sexual abuse in the third degree in violation of Code
  4 32 section 709.4; lascivious acts with a child in violation of
  4 33 Code section 709.8; assault with intent to commit sexual abuse
  4 34 in violation of Code section 709.11; indecent contact with a
  4 35 child in violation of Code section 709.12; lascivious conduct
  5  1 with a minor in violation of Code section 709.14; sexual
  5  2 exploitation by a counselor, therapist, or school employee in
  5  3 violation of Code section 709.15; sexual misconduct with a
  5  4 juvenile in violation of Code section 709.16, subsection 2;
  5  5 kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Code section
  5  6 710.2; kidnapping in the second degree in violation of Code
  5  7 section 710.3; kidnapping in the third degree in violation of
  5  8 Code section 710.4; human trafficking in violation of Code
  5  9 section 710A.2; incest in violation of Code section 726.2; and
  5 10 sexual exploitation of a minor in violation of Code section
  5 11 728.12. Under current law for the preceding offenses, an
  5 12 information or indictment  committed on or with a person who
  5 13 is under 18 years of age shall be found within 10 years after
  5 14 the person upon whom the offense is committed attains 18 years
  5 15 of age, or if the person against whom the information or
  5 16 indictment is sought is identified through the use of a DNA
  5 17 profile, an information or indictment shall be found within
  5 18 three years from the date the person is identified by the
  5 19 person's DNA profile, whichever is later.

  5 21 information or indictment for kidnapping in the first, second,

  5 23 age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  5 24 the offense. Under current law for kidnapping offenses, the

  5  3 violation of Code section 709.15; sexual misconduct with a
  5  4 juvenile in violation of Code section 709.16, subsection 2;
  5  5 kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Code section
  5  6 710.2; kidnapping in the second degree in violation of Code
  5  7 section 710.3; kidnapping in the third degree in violation of
  5  8 Code section 710.4; human trafficking in violation of Code
  5  9 section 710A.2; incest in violation of Code section 726.2; and
  5 10 sexual exploitation of a minor in violation of Code section
  5 11 728.12. Under current law for the preceding offenses, an
  5 12 information or indictment  committed on or with a person who
  5 13 is under 18 years of age shall be found within 10 years after
  5 14 the person upon whom the offense is committed attains 18 years
  5 15 of age, or if the person against whom the information or
  5 16 indictment is sought is identified through the use of a DNA
  5 17 profile, an information or indictment shall be found within
  5 18 three years from the date the person is identified by the
  5 19 person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 20    The amendment to Code section 802.2C provides that an
  5 21 information or indictment for kidnapping in the first, second,
  5 22 or third degree committed on or with a person who is under the
  5 23 age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  5 24 the offense. Under current law for kidnapping offenses, the
  5 25 information or indictment for an offense committed on or with
  5 26 a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be

  5  9 section 710A.2; incest in violation of Code section 726.2; and
  5 10 sexual exploitation of a minor in violation of Code section
  5 11 728.12. Under current law for the preceding offenses, an
  5 12 information or indictment  committed on or with a person who
  5 13 is under 18 years of age shall be found within 10 years after
  5 14 the person upon whom the offense is committed attains 18 years
  5 15 of age, or if the person against whom the information or
  5 16 indictment is sought is identified through the use of a DNA
  5 17 profile, an information or indictment shall be found within
  5 18 three years from the date the person is identified by the
  5 19 person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 20    The amendment to Code section 802.2C provides that an
  5 21 information or indictment for kidnapping in the first, second,
  5 22 or third degree committed on or with a person who is under the
  5 23 age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  5 24 the offense. Under current law for kidnapping offenses, the
  5 25 information or indictment for an offense committed on or with
  5 26 a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  5 27 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense
  5 28 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  5 29 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  5 30 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  5 31 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  5 32 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
  5 33    The amendment to Code section 802.2D provides that an
  5 34 information or indictment for human trafficking in violation of
  5 35 Code section 710A.2, committed on or with a person who is under
  6  1 the age of 18 years may be found at any time after commission of
  6  2 the offense. Under current law for human trafficking offenses,
  6  3 the information or indictment for an offense committed on or
  6  4 with a person who is under the age of 18 years of age, shall be
  6  5 found within 10 years after the person upon whom the offense

  6  6 is committed attains 18 years of age, or if the person against
  6  7 whom the information or indictment is sought is identified
  6  8 through the use of a DNA profile, an information or indictment
  6  9 shall be found within three years from the date the person is
  6 10 identified by the person's DNA profile, whichever is later.
